### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî fix(charly): plugin-verb tests are self-contained ‚Äî TestMain preloads the builtin plugin schemas

Test-only change (no production behavior). A new `TestMain` in the charly package runs
the sync.Once `loadBuiltinPluginUnits()` ‚Äî the builtin plugin-schema load the binary does
at boot ‚Äî BEFORE any test, so plugin-verb validation (`validateAuthoredPluginInput`) sees
the builtin `#<Word>Input` defs in EVERY test, not only when a sibling test
(`plugin_external_test.go`) happens to trigger the global sync.Once-filled `pluginSchemas`
first. Before this, `TestRunPluginVerb_Dispatch` and friends passed in the full
`go test ./...` suite but FAILED in a narrow `-run` subset (`no input def registered
(schema not loaded)`) ‚Äî surfaced while landing the external-charly-verb dispatch enabler
(v2026.173.1058) and recorded there as a non-blocking follow-up. The loader is idempotent
(`builtinGateOnce`), so the existing sibling call is now a no-op. Gate: `go test` ‚Äî the
previously-failing subset passes AND the full suite stays green; no bed (no production
code path touched).

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): external-charly-verb dispatch ‚Äî a live verb word can be served by an out-of-process provider (no #Op migration)

The Phase-1 enabler that makes verb externalization ADDITIVE, not a schema migration.
A live verb word (cdp/kube/vnc/‚Ä¶) is authored in `#Op` (`kube: apply`, `namespace: demo`)
and dispatched in `checkrun.go` via `providerRegistry.ResolveVerb`. Previously a resolved
provider that was NOT a `CheckVerbProvider` (i.e. out-of-process) was SKIPPED with "no
in-process check handler". Now it routes to the Invoke envelope: the new shared
`invokeVerbProvider` (`provider_checkenv.go`) marshals the FULL Op + the check env and
calls `prov.Invoke(OpRun)`, decoding the `pluginCheckResult` ‚Äî the SAME path the generic
`plugin:` verb uses (factored out of `runPluginVerb`, R3: two callers now).

The key consequence (corrects an earlier wrong assumption that verb extraction needs an
authoring migration): because the plugin is handed the full Op as `params_json`, a verb's
params STAY authored in `#Op` with NO `charly migrate` step and NO cross-repo corpus
sweep when its implementation moves out-of-tree ‚Äî the plugin reads them from the Op,
exactly as the in-proc `runCharlyVerb` did. `TestInvokeVerbProvider_ExternalCharlyVerb`
proves it: a non-`CheckVerbProvider` verb provider receives `Op{Kube: apply, Namespace:
demo}` intact and its `pluginCheckResult` decodes. The `else`-branch routing is reached
only once a real external verb registers (Phase 1's first verb extraction) ‚Äî the same
"enabler now, consumer next" shape as E3-kind. R10: `go test ./...` (factoring +
no-migration unit test) + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora) + check-pod (the
builtin verb-dispatch path unregressed). Observed pre-existing follow-up: the plugin-verb
unit tests depend on global builtin-schema state loaded by a sibling test (pass in the
full suite, fail in a narrow `-run` subset) ‚Äî its own future cutover (make them
self-contained), non-blocking here.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): E3-deploy ‚Äî an external deploy provider drives the deploy flow via the E3b reverse channel

The consumer of E3b: the deploy flow can now resolve a `target:` to an OUT-OF-PROCESS
deploy provider (a grpcProvider, Invoke-only ‚Äî not a typed DeployTargetProvider) and run
it. `ResolveTarget` (unified_targets.go) keeps the typed path for the built-in targets
(local/vm/pod/k8s/android) and routes an external deploy provider to a new
`externalDeployTarget` adapter (deploy_target_external.go) ‚Äî a `UnifiedDeployTarget`
whose `Add` calls `grpcProvider.InvokeWithExecutor` with the host's executor served on
the go-plugin broker, so the plugin dials back to run the deployment's ops on the real
venue (the E3b reverse channel).

Proven END-TO-END through the deploy flow: `TestExternalDeployPlugin_ReverseChannelEnd
ToEnd` now also registers the external provider, resolves `target: exampledeploy` through
`ResolveTarget` to the `externalDeployTarget` adapter, and confirms `adapter.Add` drives
the same reverse channel (the plugin's script reaches the host executor) ‚Äî not just a
direct `InvokeWithExecutor`. R10: `go test ./...` (the real-plugin deploy-flow test) +
`charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 ‚Äî built-in deploy routing unregressed)
+ check-pod (a pod deploy exercises ResolveTarget). The remaining external deploy
lifecycle ‚Äî `Del`/`Test`/`Update` over the wire with reverse-op recording, live checks,
and plan-diff update ‚Äî rides with the Phase-3 promotion of a real built-in deploy target
to an external plugin; the adapter errors clearly on those for now.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): E3b ‚Äî the host-served ExecutorService reverse channel (out-of-process deploy/step/builder)

The last Phase-0 enabler: an OUT-OF-PROCESS deploy/step/builder plugin can now drive the
host's live `DeployExecutor` (shell/SSH on the venue) ‚Äî which holds OS resources that
cannot cross a process boundary ‚Äî by calling BACK to the host over a go-plugin broker
reverse channel. New proto `ExecutorService{Venue,RunSystem,RunUser}` +
`InvokeRequest.executor_broker_id` (regenerated via `task proto:gen`). Host:
`executorReverseServer` (plugin_executor_reverse.go) serves it by delegating to a
`DeployExecutor`; `grpcProvider.InvokeWithExecutor` (plugin_grpc.go) stands the server
up on `g.conn.Broker` for the synchronous Invoke and passes the broker id. SDK:
`Executor` + `ExecutorFromInvoke` (plugin/sdk/executor.go) dial that id; sdk.go captures
the go-plugin broker on BOTH sides (`servedBroker` plugin-side, `Conn.Broker` host-side
‚Äî previously discarded). Built-in providers keep the typed `DeployExecutor` directly
(no wire).

Proven END-TO-END on real code: `candy/plugin-example-deploy` (its own Go module) is
host-built and served out-of-process over `LocalTransport`; `TestExternalDeployPlugin_
ReverseChannelEndToEnd` drives `InvokeWithExecutor`, the plugin dials back through the
broker, runs a marker script, and it reaches the host's executor. Plus
`TestExecutorReverseServer_DelegatesToExecutor` (the host server in isolation). Every
piece is exercised ‚Äî no dead code. R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the e2e real-plugin test)
+ `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) + check-pod (no transport
regression). The deploy-flow integration that lets a real `deploy:` USE an external
provider (`ResolveTarget` ‚Üí an `externalDeployTarget` adapter ‚Üí `InvokeWithExecutor`) is
the E3-deploy consumer, riding with the Phase-3 deploy-target extraction.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): the command-provider seam ‚Äî a 6th provider class contributes CLI subcommands

Phase-0 scaffolding: charly's CLI gains a sixth provider class, `command`, so a
non-machinery command can be contributed by its provider (and, in time, an out-of-tree
plugin) instead of being hardcoded on the Kong root. New `ClassCommand` (provider.go +
the `providerClasses` closed set) and `CommandProvider` interface (provider_command.go)
‚Äî `KongCommand() any` returns a pointer to a struct whose fields Kong merges into the
grammar via `kong.Plugins`; `builtinCommandBase` supplies the in-proc-only Provider
half. The CLI struct (main.go) embeds `kong.Plugins`, populated from
`collectCommandPlugins()` (enumerates every registered `CommandProvider`, stable order)
immediately before `kong.Parse`. The machinery commands (box/migrate/__plugin/settings/
version/doctor/clean/candy) stay hardcoded on the CLI struct.

The seam is dormant today ‚Äî zero command providers ‚Äî so the CLI is byte-for-byte the
same (`charly --help` unchanged); the ~27 non-machinery command migrations ride with
their domains in Phase 1-4 (check/feature with verbs, vm/domain with kinds, the
deploy-lifecycle commands with deploy targets), each becoming a `command` provider +
(when it ships built-in) a `providers:` manifest entry. Coverage:
`TestCommandSeam_PluginCommandInjected` registers a fake command provider and proves
its subcommand is collected and embedded into the REAL CLI grammar (`charly
<probe>` parses and selects it) ‚Äî the seam works end-to-end even while empty. R10:
`go test ./...` + `charly box validate` + `charly --help`/`version` smoke + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): registry from charly.yml ‚Äî built-in provider registration driven by the embedded `providers:` manifest

Cutover B of "registry from charly.yml" (the consolidation was Cutover A): built-in
provider registration is now DRIVEN by a `providers:` manifest in the embedded
charly.yml, not a hardcoded Go list. New `providers` document directive (schema/
node.cue `#NodeDoc` + the exclusion regex, regenerated into `spec.DocDirectives` via
`task cue:gen`) ‚Äî `providers: { <class>: [<word>, ‚Ä¶] }` mapping each provider class
(kind/verb/deploy/step/builder) to the reserved words it contributes. The embedded
charly.yml carries the full manifest (all 66 built-ins). `registry_bootstrap.go`'s
`init()` now: parses ONLY the `providers:` directive from `embeddedCharlyDefaults` via
a minimal yaml decode (`parseEmbeddedProviderManifest` ‚Äî deliberately not the full
node-form loader, which needs the very kind providers this manifest registers, the
bootstrap circularity), gates the manifest ‚áÑ compiled-in instances into exact
bijection (`manifestInstanceProblems` ‚Äî a manifest entry with no instance, or an
instance no manifest entry names, both panic loudly), then registers exactly the
providers the manifest names. The Go `builtinProviderInstances` list remains only as
the instance SUPPLIER (Go types can't be constructed from data); the manifest is the
membership AUTHORITY. The node-form loader skips `providers:` as a recognized directive
(the corpus still validates).

Coverage: `TestProviderManifest_EnforcedBijection` proves the shipped manifest agrees
with the instances, that it drove registration (every manifest provider resolves in
the registry), and that the bijection catches BOTH an omitted entry and a stray entry.
R10: `go test ./...` (the init panics at startup on any manifest/instance break) +
`charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 ‚Äî loader accepts the directive) +
check-pod. External providers continue to declare via `plugin:` candy blocks (already
charly.yml); this cutover covers the built-ins.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî refactor(charly): consolidate the 5 per-class provider-registration init()s into one site

Structural foundation for the charly.yml-declared provider manifest (the next cutover,
"registry from charly.yml"): the five per-class registration `init()`s (verb / kind /
deploy / step / builder_builtins.go) ‚Äî each a `for _, p := range []‚Ä¶Provider{‚Ä¶}
{ RegisterBuiltinProvider(p) }` loop plus its own bijection gate ‚Äî are replaced by ONE
list `builtinProviderInstances []Provider` (all 66 compiled-in providers) and ONE
`init()` in registry_bootstrap.go that registers them all, then runs every per-class
bijection gate (verb-provider, method-allowlist, kind-provider, deploy-target, step)
in sequence. Each gate still runs after ALL registration, so it observes the full
registry ‚Äî the same after-registration guarantee each per-class init() gave for its
own class, now in one place. Behavior-identical (same 66 providers, same gates); the
orphaned `spec` imports in verb/kind_builtins.go are removed. This single registration
site is what the upcoming manifest will data-drive (the loop iterates the manifest
instead of the hardcoded list). R10: `go test ./...` (the gates panic at init if any
provider failed to register) + corpus validate (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): E4 ‚Äî live-verb providers self-describe their method contract (delete the central switch + liveVerbDispatch)

Phase-0 enabler of the maximal-out-of-tree program: each live-container verb (cdp/wl/
dbus/vnc/mcp/record/spice/libvirt/kube/adb/appium) now OWNS its method contract on its
provider, replacing the central per-verb dispatch. New `LiveVerbProvider` interface
(provider_verb.go) ‚Äî `Methods() map[string]methodSpec` + `MethodField(*Op) string`;
each provider implements it (verb_method_contract.go) returning its existing
`<verb>Methods` map + its method-selector field. Deleted: the 10-case
`validateCharlyVerb` switch (validate_check.go ‚Äî now a single
`providerRegistry.ResolveVerb` ‚Üí `LiveVerbProvider` lookup) and the central
`liveVerbDispatch` map (reserved_registry.go). The method-allowlist bijection gate
(`checkMethodAllowlists`) now reads each allowlist from the registered provider and
runs in the verb-registration `init()` (after registration, mirroring
`checkVerbProviderBijection` ‚Äî avoids the alphabetical init-order race).

**Closes a validation gap (R1):** `liveVerbDispatch` carried `kube` but the old
`validateCharlyVerb` switch omitted it, so `kubeMethods`' required-modifier specs
(`apply`‚ÜíManifest, `wait-ready`‚Üí{Kind,Name}, `lb-external-ip`‚Üí{Namespace,Name},
`delete`‚ÜíManifest, `raw`‚ÜíResource) were never validated at config time. The generic
per-provider check covers ALL live verbs uniformly, so kube is now config-validated;
the corpus (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) confirms no config ‚Äî incl. the k3s-server /
k3s-agent kube checks ‚Äî relied on the gap.

The `<verb>Methods` maps stay in checkrun_charly_verbs.go (the verb's dispatch data,
used by `runCharlyVerb`) but are now OWNED by their providers via `Methods()`. The
remaining E4 surfaces ‚Äî serving the serializable method contract over the plugin
`Describe` channel, and physically relocating each verb's map + `.cue` into a dedicated
plugin unit ‚Äî ride with each verb's extraction in Phase 1 (where an external verb
actually exercises the over-the-wire path; building it now would be untested dead
scaffolding). R10: `go test ./...` + corpus validate (repo + fedora) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî feat(charly): E3 ‚Äî the kind-class out-of-proc Invoke envelope (external plugin kinds)

First slice of the maximal-out-of-tree "every kind is a plugin" program (plan: `~/.claude/plans/can-ypu-please-
make-hidden-penguin.md`): generalize the verb dual-path (typed in-proc fast / serializable Invoke envelope) to
the KIND class. A built-in kind keeps the typed `KindProvider.DecodeNode` fast path (no JSON ‚Äî the perf-gate
benchmark measured the envelope at 7.6¬µs / 76 allocs per op, so the per-entity decode hot path MUST stay
typed); an EXTERNAL plugin kind (which the core has no Go type for) now decodes out-of-process via its
`Invoke(Op: OpLoad)` envelope. Three additive pieces: (1) `classifyDisc` (node_parse.go) recognizes a
plugin-contributed kind dynamically via `providerRegistry.ResolveKind` ‚Äî only for non-core discriminators, so
the hot path is untouched (it was a "no discriminator" hard error before); (2) `runPluginKind`
(provider_kind_invoke.go) ‚Äî the kind-class analogue of `runPluginVerb`: assemble the node body ‚Üí YAML‚ÜíJSON ‚Üí
`validateAuthoredPluginInput(ClassKind, ‚Ä¶)` against the plugin's served `.cue` ‚Üí `Invoke` ‚Üí store the canonical
entity in the new host-internal `UnifiedFile.PluginKinds` slot; (3) `normalizeNodeInto` branches builtin
(`DecodeNode`) / external (`runPluginKind`). `builtinKindBase.Invoke` still errors "in-process only".

Coverage: `TestRunPluginKind_DecodesViaEnvelope` exercises the whole new path LIVE (recognition ‚Üí validation ‚Üí
envelope decode ‚Üí store) and FAILS without the implementation; the gRPC transport itself is proven by reuse
(the verb class, `TestExternalPluginEndToEnd`). R10: `go test ./...` + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora,
exit 0 ‚Äî the additive loader change does not regress the core kind path) + check-pod. Follow-ups (own cutovers):
the deploy/step/builder envelopes + E3b's `ExecutorService` reverse-channel; a dedicated external-kind plugin
bed for end-to-end gRPC-kind coverage; then Phase 1‚Äì4 extractions.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî refactor(charly): trim two now-unnecessary validate-path checks (post-E1; BF1 folded in)

Two Go validation checks are no longer needed. (1) `validateDownloadTask`'s `extract` enum check + the
`taskExtractValid` map (validate.go) ‚Äî REDUNDANT now that E1's step gate (`validateNodeFormSteps`) types every
plan step against the closed `#Op`, whose `extract:` enum (_common.cue) rejects a bad value at `charly box
validate` (proven: a download step with `extract: zzbogus` now exits 1 via the CUE step gate ALONE). The
cross-field rules in `validateDownloadTask` STAY in Go ‚Äî `download:` requires a URL, `to:` required unless
`extract: sh` (proven: removing `to:` still errors `download requires to: destination`). (2) `validate_check.go`'s
`if verb == "port" && c.Port == 0` ‚Äî STRUCTURALLY DEAD: `VerbsSet` (charly_methods.go) classifies an op as the
`port` verb ONLY when `c.Port != 0`, so `verb=="port"` already implies `Port!=0` ‚Äî the branch never fired
(this is the former Wave-A **BF1**). Reworded its comment.

**RDD CORRECTION** of the planned "lift the per-task validators into `#RunOp` arms": the `#Op` schema comment
states exactly-one-verb + the cross-field required-modifier rules are DELIBERATELY kept in Go (CUE closes the
field set + types/enums each field; Go owns cross-field). Moving them into a CUE `#RunOp` disjunction would
contradict that documented design AND degrade error messages ‚Äî a disjunction failure reports a cryptic
"empty disjunction" where the Go validators give precise, actionable messages (`download requires to:
destination unless extract: sh`). So the clean post-E1 deletion is the FIELD-LEVEL extract enum (now in CUE) +
the dead port check; cross-field validation stays in Go where it reads clearly and errors well. Recognizing
that the existing CUE-field-level / Go-cross-field split is already clean is an RDD correction, NOT narrowing
(same class as the P1/P4 corrections).

R10: go test ./... + charly box validate (repo + box/fedora + box/ubuntu, exit 0; bad extract still rejected by
the CUE gate, download‚Üíto: still rejected by Go) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî fix(charly): CUE validates plan-step Op fields ‚Äî close the silent-typo-acceptance gap (E1)

Node-form steps are SIBLING nodes (`<name>: {candy: ‚Ä¶, <step>: {run: ‚Ä¶}}`); the loader folds them into the
entity's `plan:` only at decode (`assembleEntityBody`), and decode is LENIENT (drops unknown keys). So the
closed `#Step`/`#Op` schema NEVER saw a candy/check plan step ‚Äî an unknown Op field (a typo like `donwload:`)
or a bad enum on a step PASSED `charly box validate` silently, then dropped at runtime (a latent bug). Proven:
an injected `zz_unknown_op_field` on a candy step exited 0 before this fix.

Fix: `validateNodeFormSteps` (cue_schema.go) re-parses each node-form manifest, folds every entity's (and
nested member's) step children into `plan:` via the existing `assembleEntityBody`, and types EACH step against
the closed `#Step` (which embeds the closed `#Op`). Wired into BOTH validate paths via ONE shared helper (R3):
`validateCandyManifestCUE` (candies) and `validateProjectCUESchemas`' node-form branch (boxes / pods / deploys
/ check beds ‚Äî previously SKIPPED there, only load-gated by `#NodeDoc`, which accepts step children as `_`). We
validate the STEPS, not the whole entity against its `#Kind`: a `vm:`/`pod:` DEPLOY block carries
deploy-envelope fields (`disposable`/`lifecycle`/`from`/`install_opts`) the workload `#Kind` does not model
(those are `#NodeDoc`'s deploy arm), so whole-entity validation false-positives (RDD-found on
`check-ubuntu-debootstrap-vm`). Steps-only is clean across the whole corpus (189 candies + every box/bed, 0
false positives) AND rejects a typo'd Op field on a candy step AND on a check-bed step (both exit 1 naming the
field). Also corrected the stale `schema/node.cue` comment that named a nonexistent `decodeAndValidateEntityCUE`
and claimed decode types steps against `#Step` (it does not ‚Äî R1), and updated `node_validate_test.go`'s fixture
off the legacy inline `package:`/`plan:`-as-fields form (which `parseNodeTree` rejects ‚Üí `charly migrate`) to
the real child-node form. New `TestNodeFormSteps_RejectsStepTypo` is the check-coverage that fails without the
fix. R10: `go test ./...` + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora + box/ubuntu, exit 0) + check-pod.

The additive step-typo gate (no Go validator deleted yet) ‚Äî the prerequisite for lifting the load-bearing Go
per-task validators (validateDownloadTask/‚Ä¶) into closed `#RunOp` arms (the next cutover, E1 step 2).

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî refactor(charly): delete validateAgentCatalog ‚Äî redundant with the closed CUE schema (P1a)

The Go `validateAgentCatalog` (unified.go) checked every `kind:agent` entry's `output_format` against
`{"", "stream-json"}` at load. But `agent.cue` already declares `output_format: *"" | "stream-json"` as a
CLOSED disjunction under the closed `#NodeDoc` gate, and `validateNodeDocCUE` rejects an illegal value at
LOAD (non-concrete `Validate()` catches the disjunction conflict ‚Üí bottom) ‚Äî BEFORE `validateAgentCatalog`
ever ran. RDD-proven: the new `TestNodeDoc_AgentOutputFormat_RejectedByCUE` shows the CUE gate rejects
`output_format: bogus` and accepts `stream-json`, INDEPENDENT of the Go validator. Deleted: the validator +
its `LoadUnified` call + the now-orphaned `AgentOutputFormatPlain` constant (its only user was the validator)
+ the 3 `agent_config_test.go` tests for it (their intent is now the CUE-gate test). `AgentOutputFormatStreamJSON`
stays (check_loop.go uses it); its const comment now points at the CUE source of truth. R10: the new CUE test
+ `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 ‚Äî real agent configs validate without the Go check) +
check-pod (the edited central loader deploys). Wave-1 **P1a** of the charly-core-externalization program ‚Äî the
ONLY clean externalization in the audit's "P1" bundle; RDD found the other 7 P1 sub-items genuinely CORE
(computed CPU defaults, go-flags CLI tags, runtime constructor defaults, behavior switches, cross-field
validation) ‚Äî recognizing that is an RDD correction, not narrowing.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî fix(charly): `charly bundle del <pod>` was broken ‚Äî record-free teardown via `charly remove`

`charly bundle del <pod>` ALWAYS errored `"no container deploy named X in ledger"`. RCA: `PodUnifiedTarget.Del`
(unified_targets_pod.go) was built on a ledger-DeployRecord teardown model that pods never use ‚Äî the ONLY
DeployRecord writer is `VmDeployTarget` (deploy_target_vm.go:181, `Target="vm:"+name`); a pod bakes its candies
into an overlay image and persists charly.yml state, writing NO deploy record. So `findContainerDeploy` always
returned nil and Del errored before tearing anything down (the bug never surfaced because the check beds tear
down with `charly remove`, not `charly bundle del`). The path was also INCOMPLETE ‚Äî it stopped+rm'd the
container but never removed the quadlet or the charly.yml entry, and its overlay check
(`strings.HasSuffix(ref, "-overlay")`) couldn't match the real `<name>-overlay:<tag>` ref.

Fixed: Del is now RECORD-FREE. It delegates the container + quadlet + sidecar + charly.yml cleanup to the
canonical `charly remove` path (consistent with the sibling lifecycle delegations Start/Stop/Update ‚Äî R3), then
drops the deploy's synthesized `<name>-overlay:*` images (the one extra `bundle del` does over `charly remove`;
a shared base ref is never named that, so it is preserved) and cancels any ephemeral TTL lifecycle. DELETED the
dead `findContainerDeploy` (Del was its only caller) and corrected the stale install_ledger.go Target-field
comment (the same false `container:<name>` claim ‚Äî R5). New regression test
`TestPodUnifiedTarget_Del_DelegatesToRemove` asserts the `remove <name>` delegation.

R10 (live, disposable check-pod): `bundle add check-pod` + config + start ‚Üí running; `bundle del check-pod` ‚Üí
EXIT 0, container removed + quadlet removed + charly.yml entry cleaned + base image preserved (was: always
errored). `go test ./...` (incl. the new test) + `task build:charly` green. Surfaced during the
charly-core-externalization triage (the findContainerDeploy follow-up, upgraded from a dead-code note to a real
bug).

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî refactor(charly): collapse the duplicated volume host-path strategy into one helper (PP5)

`ResolveVolumeBacking` (deploy.go) carried the bind/encrypted host-path strategy switch TWICE ‚Äî once for
label-matched volumes (keyed by the short name) and once for deploy-only volumes (keyed by the config name) ‚Äî
byte-identical apart from that name argument. Extracted to ONE `resolveVolumeHostPath(dv, name, storageDir,
encStoragePath, volumesPath)` helper (R3); both passes call it. Behavior-identical (the only varying input is
now an explicit parameter); no exported-signature change, callers unchanged. The gocryptfs encrypted LIFECYCLE
stays core (a volume-backing provider class was correctly deferred ‚Äî single backend, deeply wired into
start/quadlet/credential). Also FIXED a standing R1 divergence: two `enc_test.go` comments promised tests at
`deploy_test.go (TestResolveVolumeBacking*)` that never existed ‚Äî WRITTEN now (table-driven
`TestResolveVolumeBacking_HostPath` covering bind/encrypted √ó default/host, plus `TestResolveVolumeBacking`
covering named-fallthrough + label-matched + deploy-only), making the comments true. R10: go test (the new
tests) + check-pod (ResolveVolumeBacking drives every pod deploy, fresh `charly update`). Wave-1 **PP5** of the
charly-core-externalization program.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî refactor(charly): delete the dead deploy-target legacy-spelling alias residue (P3)

EDGE-INHERIT / schema-v4 left runtime alias-following for the legacy deploy-target spellings
(`container`‚Üí`pod`, `kubernetes`‚Üí`k8s`, `host`‚Üí`local`), but the runtime NEVER sees them: `BundleNode.Target`
is set only by `bundleTargetForDisc` from the node-form kind at the edge (always canonical
pod|vm|k8s|local|android), `charly migrate` (schema-v4 + target-local) rewrites the legacy spellings
on-disk, and the loader hard-rejects un-migrated configs. The alias-following was pure dead
belt-and-suspenders. Deleted: the legacy-spelling switch arms in `classifyTarget` (deploy_tree.go) and
`classifyNodeTarget` (bundle_add_cmd.go); the now-no-op `canonicalDeployWord` (unified_targets.go); the three
`RegisterBuiltinAlias(ClassDeployTarget, ‚Ä¶)` calls (deploy_builtins.go); and ‚Äî deploy-target being its ONLY
user ‚Äî the whole registry alias mechanism (the `aliases` map, `RegisterBuiltinAlias`, and `resolve`'s alias
branch in provider_registry.go). Canonical dispatch is unchanged (`resolve` is a plain byKey lookup;
`checkDeployProviderBijection` iterates canonical words). Also corrected a stale migration-status comment that
claimed kinds/steps/builders are "still switch-driven" (C2/C4/C5 landed). KEPT (separate concerns, not this
claim): the name-based fallbacks (a deploy literally NAMED `host`/`local` ‚Üí local) and the persisted-ledger
`container:`-key reader `findContainerDeploy` (deploy-record state-format, its own future assessment).

R10: go test ./... + check-pod + check-local (each resolves its canonical target through the now alias-free
registry, on a fresh `charly update`). Wave-1 **P3** of the charly-core-externalization program ‚Äî corrected
from the audit's "route through the registry" (which assumed the aliases were live) to an R5 dead-residue
deletion after RDD proved them unreachable.

### 2026-06-22 ‚Äî fix(charly): enforce the plugin protocol-version gate on connect (was claimed, never performed)

`buildUnit` (the client-side construction lifting a connected plugin's `Describe` reply into a
`*PluginUnit`) read only `caps.GetProvided()` + `caps.GetSchemaCue()` and SILENTLY DISCARDED the
`Capabilities.protocol_version` + `calver` fields the server sends ‚Äî while a comment in `connectAndDescribe`
asserted "a gross mismatch is a readable refusal rather than a wire panic." No refusal code existed: a plugin
built against a different charly proto/SDK connected silently and failed later as a wire panic. Fixed:
`buildUnit` now enforces `caps.GetProtocolVersion() == sdk.ProtocolVersion` and refuses a mismatch with a
readable error naming the plugin's protocol, its (advisory) CalVer, and the host's required protocol. CalVer
is NOT an equality gate ‚Äî plugins are independent repos at independent CalVers, and a same-host builtin served
out-of-process may advertise an empty CalVer (identical binary) ‚Äî so it is surfaced in the diagnostic only.
The false comment is replaced with a truthful one; `TestBuildUnitRefusesProtocolMismatch` covers the refusal,
`TestPluginGRPCRoundTrip` the accept path. R10: `check-pod` (the external out-of-tree plugin advertises the
matching protocol ‚Üí bed green with the gate active). Wave-1 **PE4** of the charly-core-externalization
program (`~/.claude/plans/charly-core-externalization.md`).

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî fix(charly): `charly vm ssh` connects via the managed ssh_config alias, not `localhost:2222` (cutover-B finding)

`charly vm ssh <name>` reconstructed the ssh invocation by hand ‚Äî `ssh -p <port> <user>@localhost`, the port
DEFAULTING to 2222 and resolved only from the vm spec's `SSH.Port`. For a `port_auto` VM the auto-allocated host
port lives in `VmDeployState`, NOT the spec, so the resolution missed it and fell back to `localhost:2222` ‚Äî
connecting to the wrong port. Fixed: `vm ssh` now execs `ssh <vmName>`, the MANAGED ssh_config Host alias
(`charly-<box>[-<instance>]`) published at `charly vm create` (`publishVmSshAlias`), which resolves the user,
the host port (including the auto-allocated one), and the generated key from `~/.config/charly/ssh_config`. This
DELETES the duplicate manual port/key resolution (R3 ‚Äî the alias is the single managed SSH interface); `-l`/`-p`
still override. Live-verified: on a fresh `port_auto` k3s-vm (resolved port 35423, not 2222), `charly vm ssh
k3s-vm echo ‚Ä¶` connected through the alias and ran the command. Found during cutover B's cachyos-vm investigation.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî fix(charly): drop the stale `host` (C) + `box` (D) kind words from the wrong-kind-child gate

EDGE-INHERIT residual cleanup (a cutover-C + cutover-D follow-up). The wrong-kind-child gate's HARDCODED
kind lists had drifted: `node_parse.go` listed `host` among the deployable kinds (cutover C removed the
`host:` venue kind) and `box` among the non-deployable kinds (cutover D merged `box:` into `candy:`), and
`node_bundle.go`'s resource-member error listed `host`. Corrected to the current kinds ‚Äî deployable:
`pod/vm/k8s/local/android/group`; non-deployable: `candy/distro/‚Ä¶`; resource members:
`pod/vm/k8s/local/android`. `resourceKindSet` itself is CUE-derived (`spec.ResourceKinds`) and was already
correct ‚Äî only the hardcoded error/comment STRINGS were stale, so there is no behavior change (an invalid
config was already rejected; only the message text was wrong). Live-verified: `charly box validate` on a
wrong-kind-child config now emits the corrected list. The check skill's reserved-kind list drops `host` too.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover D ‚Äî the `box:` KIND merged into `candy:` (`base:`/`from:` presence = image)

The fourth and LARGEST EDGE-INHERIT cutover, completing the program ("kinds live only at config EDGES").
The `box:` KIND keyword is ELIMINATED ‚Äî merged INTO `candy:`. There is now ONE entity kind: a `candy:` node
carrying `base:` (an external base) or `from:` (a builder ref) is a full IMAGE (the former `box:`); a `candy:`
with neither is a LAYER fragment. The `charly box build/validate/...` COMMAND family is UNCHANGED (a command,
not a kind ‚Äî like `charly bundle` survived cutover B).

**The loader.** `candyKind.DecodeNode` routes a `candy:` node by `candyIsImage` (the `base` OR `from` marker
‚Äî the corpus has 75 boxes with `base:`, 4 bootstrap builders with `from: builder:‚Ä¶` and no base, and zero
layers using `from:`) into `uf.Box` (BoxConfig) vs `uf.Candy` (InlineCandy) ‚Äî the existing SEPARATE maps, so
the box‚äïcandy name reuses (redis, nvidia, jupyter, ‚Ä¶) need ZERO renames. `boxKind` is deleted; `box` leaves
`_reservedNode`/`#Node`.

**The schema ‚Äî the implicit-discriminator hazard the design panel flagged, resolved.** A raw `(#Candy | #Box)`
disjunction is NOT concretely validatable: in CUE a required-but-absent field is INCOMPLETE, not BOTTOM, so a
no-base/no-from layer never eliminates the image arm. Fix: `#Image: #Box & ({base!} | {from!})` (the image arm
REQUIRES base‚äªfrom) and `#CandyValue: (*#Candy | #Image)` ‚Äî the `*#Candy` DEFAULT resolves it (an image carries
base/from ‚Üí bottoms closed `#Candy` ‚Üí `#Image`; a layer ‚Üí the default `#Candy` wins). `candy.cue`'s `from:` is
removed (it is now an image marker on `#Box`).

**The migration.** New `box-to-candy` step (`renameBoxDisc`: `box:`‚Üí`candy:` at every KIND discriminator,
scoped to MAPPING-valued discriminators so a `box:` cross-ref FIELD is never touched) ‚Üí HEAD `2026.172.0006`;
the corpus is migrated + re-stamped across the superproject + all 5 `box/<distro>` submodules + the per-host
overlay.

**Four production bugs the box/candy merge surfaced, each RCA'd and fixed in this cutover:** (1) `validate.go`
validated images against the now-deleted `cueKindDef("box")` ‚Üí `box`‚Üí`#Box` re-registered as an INTERNAL
validation key (cueKindDefs is not bijective with the kind keywords); (2) the disjunction concrete-validation
(the `*#Candy` default above); (3) `renameBoxDisc` over-reached onto the `box:` IMAGE cross-ref FIELD of
`#K8s`/`#Android` ‚Üí scoped to mapping-valued discriminators; (4) `applyDiscoveredManifest` had its OWN `candy:`
discovery branch missing the `candyIsImage` check, so discovered IMAGES landed in `uf.Candy` ‚Äî breaking
`charly box list`/`box build` for every submodule (`&& !candyIsImage(gn)` added). The `AddBox` scaffold is
rewritten from the stale kind-keyed `box:` to node-form `<name>: {candy: {base:}}`. The `candy:`-as-CHILD =
composition behavior (classifyDisc's `asChild`) is correct and preserved ‚Äî an image/layer can never be a
deploy member.

Docs (CLAUDE.md + 93 SKILL.md + README) swept of the `box:` kind, with strict MUST-form authoring guidance
(an IMAGE MUST be a `candy:` carrying `base:`/`from:`; the `charly box` COMMAND is unchanged). R10 (all
fresh-rebuild gates green): check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm + check-arch-vscode-pod +
check-debian-coder-pod + check-ubuntu-coder-pod + check-cachyos-vm.

**Follow-ups found (each its own next cutover):** `#K8s`/`#Android`'s image cross-ref FIELD is still spelled
`box:` (should be `image:`, a cutover-B gap); the `host` kind word still appears in `node_parse.go`'s
wrong-kind-child error message + the check skill's reserved-kind list (a cutover-C residual).

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover C ‚Äî eliminate the `host:` venue kind; rename Calamares `group` ‚Üí `package-group`

The third EDGE-INHERIT cutover ‚Äî a ZERO-CORPUS schema refactor (the `host:` venue kind and the Calamares
`group:` both have zero on-disk usage, so there is no migration / re-stamp; the schema change is in-place,
no HEAD bump).

**C.1 ‚Äî the `host:` venue KIND is GONE.** A remote/host deploy is the `host:` FIELD on a `local:` deploy
(`local: {from: <template>, host: <user@machine>}`), never a standalone `host:` venue node. `#HostValue` +
`#HostArm` are deleted from node.cue; `host` leaves `_reservedNode` + `#ResourceKind`; the `bundleKind`
provider (its last user ‚Äî `bundle` went in cutover B, `host` now) is deleted; and the DEAD config-derived
`host` disc/target branches (`node_bundle.go` `bundleTargetForDisc`, `deploy_tree.go` `deriveChildExecutor`,
`deploy_chain.go` `appendHopForFlatPath`) are removed. The internal runtime "host" EXECUTION-venue label
(the host MACHINE ‚Äî a separate concept, not a config kind) is unchanged.

**C.2 ‚Äî the Calamares package group moves to its own `package-group:` kind.** `group:` is now UNAMBIGUOUSLY
the targetless DEPLOY group (resource members, no own workload ‚Äî the former targetless `bundle:`); the
cutover-B dual-mode shape-routing in `groupKind.DecodeNode` is gone, and a new `packageGroupKind` decodes
`#Group` into `uf.Group`. `cueKindDefs` realigned: `group`‚Üí`#Deploy`, `package-group`‚Üí`#Group` (was the
stale `group`‚Üí`#Group`, which would have validated a deploy group against the Calamares def ‚Äî a latent
zero-corpus bug fixed here). The `target.cue` `group?: [...string]` FIELD (package-group names) is unchanged.

Skills + CLAUDE.md swept of the `host:` venue kind + the `group:` dual-mode, and given strict MUST-form
authoring guidance (a host deploy MUST be `local: {host: ‚Ä¶}`; a Calamares group MUST be `package-group:`).
The migrate skill table is backfilled with the cutover-A/B step rows + the correct HEAD. R10 (all
fresh-rebuild gates green): check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover B ‚Äî `bundle:` kind eliminated; substrate kinds at the EDGE with `from:`/`image:` cross-refs

The second cutover of the EDGE-INHERIT program ("kinds live only at config EDGES, never in the middle").
The `bundle:` deploy KIND keyword is GONE: a deploy now carries its SUBSTRATE KIND directly at the edge ‚Äî
`pod:` / `vm:` / `k8s:` / `local:` / `android:` for a workload, or `group:` for a targetless group of
members. The six cross-ref FIELDS `box?`/`pod?`/`vm?`/`k8s?`/`local?`/`android?` collapse to two: `image:`
(the box/OCI image a `pod`/`k8s`/`android` RUNS ‚Äî the former `box:`) and `from:` (inherit a SAME-kind
template by name ‚Äî the former `vm:`/`k8s:`/`local:`/`android:` cross-refs). So `bundle:{box:web}`‚Üí
`pod:{image:web}`, `bundle:{vm:pg}`‚Üí`vm:{from:pg}`, and a targetless `bundle:{disposable:true,‚Ä¶}`‚Üí
`group:{‚Ä¶}`.

The substrate kinds serve DOUBLE duty (a `vm:` is EITHER a VmSpec template with `source:` OR a deploy with
`from:`/`image:`), resolved by SHAPE in the loader (`standaloneKind.DecodeNode` routes on `isDeployShape`:
a scalar disc value or a `from:`/`image:` field ‚Üí a deploy; bare ‚Üí a template); `group:` is dual-mode too
(the Calamares package group vs a targetless deploy group, routed by resource members). The RDD spike that
opened the cutover proved the CUE DISJUNCTION arm resolves template-XOR-deploy cleanly, so `VmSpec` and
`BundleNode` stay SEPARATE Go types ‚Äî the ripple is just the cross-ref fields, NOT a 480-ref restructure.
CUE `#Deploy` loses the six cross-refs (gains `from?`/`image?`); `#BundleArm`/`#BundleValue`/the `bundle`
reserved word are deleted from `node.cue`; `group` joins `#ResourceKind` (a deploy group nests members,
its Calamares-subgroup `subgroup:` being a FIELD, not a `group:` child, so no collision). The Go ripple is
the receiver-scoped cross-ref renames (`.Box`‚Üí`.Image`, `.Vm`/`.K8s`/`.Local`/`.Android`‚Üí`.From`) across
the loader, deploy targets, status collectors, and commands; `inferBundleTarget`/`setBundleCrossRef` are
rewritten (the disc IS the target ‚Äî no inference) and the `bundle` kind provider deleted. The save-path
serialization (`bundleDiscForEntity`) emits the substrate kind from `Target`.

A new idempotent `charly migrate` step `edge-inherit` (RECURSING into nested members) raises the schema
HEAD to `2026.172.0004`; the whole corpus (the main `charly.yml`, candies, every `box/<distro>` submodule,
and the per-host overlay) is migrated `bundle:`‚Üísubstrate. The earlier F3 host-overlay-pollution class
DISSOLVES ‚Äî a check-local bed is now a plain `local:` deploy node, not a `bundle:` carrying a `local:`
cross-ref. Skills + CLAUDE.md swept of the `bundle:` KIND (the `charly bundle` command + the `BundleNode`
Go type are unchanged).

The full bed-roster R10 surfaced a PRE-EXISTING VM-deploy race (NOT caused by the node-form change ‚Äî the
FIRST deploy passed on the same tree): `check-cachyos-vm`'s fresh-rebuild hit `pacman -Sy: unable to lock
database` because cloud-init's first-boot seed-package install still held `/var/lib/pacman/db.lck` ‚Äî
`WaitForCloudInit` cleared on a blank/transient `cloud-init status` read before `cloud-final.service`
finished. RCA'd and fixed GENERICALLY for every VM substrate (arch/cachyos/debian/ubuntu/fedora share the
injected `{openssh,curl,tar}` seed packages, so a cachyos-only cloud-init patch would be an R3 sibling
hack): `WaitForCloudInit` now gates on an explicit TERMINAL cloud-init state (done/error/disabled), and a
new R4 `WaitForPackageLock` sync primitive blocks the deploy until no boot-time pacman/apt/dnf process
holds the lock. R10: check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm + check-arch-vscode-pod + check-debian-coder-pod
+ check-ubuntu-coder-pod + check-cachyos-vm disposable beds pass on the fresh substrate form (the two VM
beds re-run on the package-lock fix).

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover A ‚Äî step probe verbs `k8s`/`group` renamed to `kube`/`unix_group` (no kind word mid-config)

The first cutover of the EDGE-INHERIT program ("kinds live only at config EDGES, never in the middle").
Two declarative check-step PROBE VERBS reused reserved KIND words: `k8s:` (cluster probe) collided with
the `k8s` deploy substrate, and `group:` (getent unix group / groupadd) with the Calamares `group` kind.
They are renamed to `kube:` / `unix_group:` everywhere ‚Äî the `#OpVerb` vocabulary + `#Op` fields (`.Kube`,
`.UnixGroup`, the kube verb's `kube_*` modifiers, the `#KubeMethod` enum, all regenerated from the
single-source `schema/_common.cue` via `task cue:gen`), the `VerbCatalog` + `liveVerbDispatch` registry
keys, the verb-provider registrations (`kubeVerb`/`unixGroupVerb`, `runKube`/`runUnixGroup`/`kubeMethods`),
and the CLI subcommand `charly check k8s <method>` ‚Üí `charly check kube <method>` (`KubeCmd`). The `k8s`
deploy KIND, the `k8s:` bundle cross-ref, and the Calamares `group` kind are UNTOUCHED (only the verb
namespace moved). New machine-checks `spec/TestNoKindWordAsStepVerb` + `TestNoKindWordAsOpModifier` fail the
build if any future step verb/modifier is spelled like a kind word. A new idempotent `charly migrate` step
`probe-verb-rename` (gated on `isStepNode` so only plan-step `k8s:`/`group:`/`k8s_*:` keys move, never the
deploy kind) raises the schema HEAD to `2026.172.0002`; the whole corpus (the main `charly.yml`, candies,
and every `box/<distro>` submodule) is re-stamped and the `check-k3s-vm` plan + `box/arch`'s `group: wheel`
check are migrated. Skills updated with strict MUST-form guidance (a step verb may never collide with a
kind word). Also fixes a pre-existing bed-infra bug surfaced by the R10: `persistBedDeployOverrides` no
longer persists a LOCAL bed to the global per-host overlay ‚Äî a local bed never runs `charly config` (its
only reason to seed) and its `local:` template lives in the bed's own project, so writing it poisoned every
OTHER project's overlay load (`validateCheckBeds: references local template ‚Ä¶ not defined`), breaking
concurrent `check-pod`/`check-k3s-vm` runs. Local deploys persist via the install ledger, so the skip is
lossless.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: unified plugin schema over the Describe channel ‚Äî `.cue` single source, zero builtin/external distinction

A plugin's `.cue` schema is now the SINGLE SOURCE used two ways, IDENTICALLY for a built-in (in-proc)
and an out-of-tree (out-of-proc) plugin: at DEV time `cue exp gengotypes` produces the plugin's Go param
struct (the provider decodes `plugin_input` into it, never a hand-parsed map); at RUNTIME the plugin
SERVES its `.cue` source over the Provider `Describe` RPC (the new proto `Capabilities.schema_cue` +
structured `ProvidedCapability{class,word,input_def}`), and the host splices it onto its base schema
(`base ++ plugin`) and validates every authored `plugin_input` against the plugin's def. The host NEVER
reads a candy's `schema/` dir from disk ‚Äî the schema travels WITH the plugin. Both kinds arrive as a
`PluginUnit{Providers,Schema}` from `PluginTransport.Connect` (`InProcTransport` for a builtin,
`LocalTransport` for an external), so the load/gate/validate code never branches: `registerPluginUnitSchema`
is the ONE load gate (empty / non-spliceable / missing-def ‚Üí loud failure; builtins gated at process start
via `loadBuiltinPluginUnits`, externals at connect), and `validateAuthoredPluginInput` is the ONE validator,
wired into `runPluginVerb`. The reference built-in moves into charly's module as a self-contained unit
(`charly/plugin/builtins/exampleprobe/`: schema + gen'd params + `Schema()`/`InputDefs`), and the external
example serves via the new `sdk.BuildCapabilities` (embeds + compiles its schema standalone, ships the
source). `task cue:gen` regenerates every plugin's params from its `.cue` (new `schemagen -pkg` flag + a
loop over `charly/plugin/builtins/*/schema` + the in-repo external). The check-runner now loads plugins
from the RESOLVED candy set (`ScanAllCandyWithConfig`, which includes `@github`-fetched candies and carries
each candy's `.Plugin` + `.SourceDir`) instead of `LoadUnified`'s project-local map ‚Äî so a box that vendors
all its candies via `@github` (every `box/<distro>`) loads its plugins; `buildPluginBinary` flattens an
`@github`-ref candy key to a safe binary filename. DELETED (R5): `compileBasePlusPlugin` (the disk-read
splice), `charly/schema/plugin_example.cue` + `spec.ExampleprobeInput` (the builtin-schema-in-core-spec
path), `buildProviders`, the old `validatePluginInput`, the proto `repeated string provided`. R10:
`check-pod` composes the built-in (`exampleprobe-baked`) AND the external plugin (`externalprobe-out-of-proc`)
‚Äî fresh `charly check run check-pod` PASS (steps=10), both plugins dispatching through the unified
schema-over-RPC mechanism, the external out-of-process with its marker round-tripping.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî fix(charly): bundle-node plan steps now run under `charly check live` (the pod path)

A pod bundle's OWN authored plan steps (a bed's `status-shows-pod` check, or any `check:` on the bundle
node) were SILENTLY NOT RUN under `charly check live` ‚Äî `CheckLiveCmd.Run` (the pod path) merged only the
baked candy/box plan + the per-host deploy overlay, never the PROJECT bundle's plan. The VM path
(`loadVmCheckPlans`) and the local path (`runLocalCheck`) already merged it; only the pod path diverged.
The fix mirrors them: the pod check-live composition now also merges `uf.ProjectBundleConfig()`'s bundle
plan (`projectPlan + localPlan`, the per-host overlay replacing by id) into the set. Found during C0 ‚Äî
the `exampleprobe` check had to be baked into the box plan to run on a pod bed; with this fix a
bundle-node check runs too. R10: check-pod runs `status-shows-pod` under check-live (previously absent ‚Äî
check-live went 8‚Üí10 steps, PASS); check-local's `status-shows-local` (the already-correct local path)
confirms no regression.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî refactor(charly): InstallPlan steps ‚Üí provider registry (delete 3 type-switches + dead WalkPlan)

C4 of the plugin program ‚Äî the LAST switch migration: the 3 per-step type-switches (OCI `emitStep` in
build_target_oci.go, local `execStep` in deploy_target_local.go, the VM `emitPlan` loop in
deploy_target_vm.go) are replaced by the provider registry. Each of the 12 InstallStep kinds is a
`StepProvider` (`step_builtins.go`) with `EmitOCI`/`EmitLocal`/`EmitVM` methods preserving their venue's
EXACT prior behaviour cell-by-cell ‚Äî the gate checks (RepoChange hard-errors without
`--allow-repo-changes`; services silent-skip without `--with-services`), the per-VM-cell ReverseOp
collection, and the apk/reboot per-venue skips; the per-target `emitX`/`execX` handlers are unchanged.
The dispatch sites resolve via `providerRegistry.ResolveStep(step.Kind())` and call the matching method;
a bijection (`checkStepProviderBijection`) asserts every kind has a provider. The DEAD, never-wired
`walk_plan.go` (`WalkPlan` + `StepExecutor` ‚Äî a "Phase 1 defined, Phase 2 never done" abstraction
covering only 8 of 12 kinds) is DELETED (R3). Behavior-preserving ‚Äî proven by the full install/emit/
deploy test suite. R5: `git grep 'case *ApkInstallStep:'` / `WalkPlan` / `StepExecutor` ‚Üí only
`CHANGELOG/`. R10: check-pod (OCI emit) + check-k3s-vm (VM emitPlan) + check-local (local execStep),
fresh-rebuild.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî refactor(charly): builders ‚Üí provider registry (delete BuilderImageResolver + 3 builder switches)

C5 of the plugin program: the 3 per-builder switches + the dead injected resolver are replaced by the
provider registry. Each built-in builder (aur/pixi/cargo/npm) is a `BuilderProvider`
(`builder_builtins.go`) carrying its UNCHANGED `Reverse` (teardown ops) + `CollectContext` (per-builder
stage context); `BuilderStep.Reverse` + `collectBuilderContext` resolve via
`providerRegistry.ResolveBuilder`. The aur staging special-case (the `if s.Builder == "aur"` guard in
execBuilder) becomes a `BuilderStager` method (aur ‚Üí `/tmp/aur-pkgs`). The injected
`BuilderImageResolver` func (local + vm targets, the tier-3 fallback) was NEVER wired in production ‚Äî
deleted, leaving the 2-tier override‚Üícompiled-step resolution. A custom candy builder has no provider ‚Üí
falls through (no reverse op, base context only); builders have no CUE vocabulary, so no bijection gate.
Behavior-preserving. R5: `git grep BuilderImageResolver` + the builder `case "aur":` ‚Üí only `CHANGELOG/`.
R10: `install_plan_test` exercises `Reverse` for all 4 builders through the registry (+ aur_replaces_test,
generate_test's OCI aur stage, vm_builder_xhost_test) and check-jupyter-pod builds the
`jupyter-pixi-build` stage (collectBuilderContext + the OCI pixi builder stage) live on a disposable bed.

C2 of the plugin program: the per-kind decode dispatch switch in `normalizeNodeInto` is replaced by
the provider registry. Each of the 18 authoring kinds (candy/box/sidecar/distro/builder/init/
resource/agent/group/target/module, the 5 resource-deploy kinds pod/vm/k8s/local/android, and the 2
bundle kinds bundle/host) is a `KindProvider` (`kind_builtins.go`) wrapping its UNCHANGED decode

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî refactor(charly): do-mode act dispatch ‚Üí ProvisionActor providers (delete renderProvisionScript)

C1b completes the C1 verb seam: the `renderProvisionScript` switch (the do:act create/configure
renderer for the 7 state-provision verbs file/package/service/user/group/kernel-param/mount) is

the verb via `providerRegistry.ResolveVerb` and type-asserts `ProvisionActor`; each renderer is now

the full act dispatch (resolve ‚Üí ProvisionActor ‚Üí render ‚Üí exec, with pass/fail/skip) is exercised
by a deterministic integration test (`TestRunProvisionActDispatch`, drives the real `runProvisionAct`
through a mock executor; FAILS without C1b). check-pod (fresh-rebuild live bed) confirms the modified
check-runner package integrates and runs end-to-end without regression.

built-in dispatch switches were unmigrated ‚Äî false after C1; R1 documentation-divergence fix).

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî refactor(charly): check verbs ‚Üí provider registry (delete the runOne dispatch switch)

C1 of the plugin program: the per-verb runtime DISPATCH switch in `Runner.runOne` is replaced by
the provider registry. Each of the 29 built-in check verbs (file/port/command/http/‚Ä¶ / cdp/wl/dbus/
vnc/mcp/record/spice/libvirt/k8s/adb/appium / summarize/kill / plugin) is a `CheckVerbProvider`
(`verb_builtins.go`) wrapping its UNCHANGED `r.runX` handler; `runOne` resolves the verb via
`providerRegistry.ResolveVerb` and calls `RunVerb`. A new same-init() gate
(`checkVerbProviderBijection`, run after registration to avoid the alphabetical init-order race)
asserts every check-dispatch `spec.OpVerb` has a provider ‚Äî the pure-install verbs
(mkdir/copy/write/link/download/setcap/build) are excluded (they render to install steps, not
checks; `command` is both and stays gated). Behavior-preserving: the live verbs still funnel through

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly): plugin-system foundation ‚Äî ONE unified Provider over the reserved-word registry

First cutover of the plugin program (`~/Atrapub/charly-plugin.md`): a single `Provider`
abstraction keyed by reserved word, generalizing the CUE-single-source reserved-word registry
so every kind/verb (and future deploy/step/builder) is one Provider ‚Äî in-process (built-in) OR
out-of-process (go-plugin gRPC), resolved identically by call sites (transport-invisible).

- **`provider.go` / `provider_registry.go`** ‚Äî the `Provider` interface (`Reserved`/`Class`/
  `Invoke` + the `Operation`/`Result` envelope) and `reservedProviders`, keyed by (class, word)
  because a word like `k8s` is both a kind and a verb. `RegisterBuiltinProvider` (init()) +
  `RegisterPluginProviders` (out-of-proc).
- **The generic `plugin:` check verb** ‚Äî `#OpVerb`/`#Op` gain `plugin`/`plugin_input`; `runOne`
  ‚Üí `runPluginVerb` ‚Üí `providerRegistry.ResolveVerb`. An out-of-tree plugin's verb is authorable
  without recompiling `Op`; an unresolved plugin verb FAILS (never fake-greens).
- **Plugins are candies** ‚Äî `#Candy.plugin:` (`{providers, source}`) + `validatePluginCandy`
  (a builtin provider must be compiled in); a plugin candy needs no install files. The reference
  built-in plugin `candy/plugin-example` provides + tests the `exampleprobe` verb.
- **go-plugin v1.8.0 + grpc v1.61.0 + protobuf** (grpc pinned to go-plugin's k8s-safe minimum ‚Äî
  forcing v1.81.1 downgraded `k8s.io/client-go` to alpha); `charly/plugin/proto` (the uniform
  Invoke envelope, JSON payloads so `spec` stays the single source) + `taskfiles/Proto.yml`
  (checksum-pinned protoc, reproducible); `LocalTransport` + `charly __plugin serve|list`.

Internal dispatch switches (check-verb / kind / deploy / step / builder) migrate in later
cutovers; the out-of-proc git-repo-plugin lifecycle (ExecutorTransport, runtime schema splice,
label discovery) + the bundle-overlay-step-not-running finding are the immediate follow-ups.
(The bundle-overlay-step-not-running finding has SINCE been FIXED ‚Äî the add_candy-on-pod overlay
now builds AND deterministically deploys via the persisted `resolved_image` ref; see the
`check-addcandy-pod` bed.)
R10: check-pod bakes + runs the `exampleprobe` plugin verb on a disposable bed (fresh-rebuild).
Bumps the `box/fedora` gitlink to the matching bed coverage.

### 2026-06-21 ‚Äî feat(charly): the init system is a true single-source OCI label (`ai.opencharly.init_def`)

Closes the R3 duplication where the init entrypoint + management commands lived in BOTH the embedded `init:` vocabulary (build-time, but its `entrypoint:`/`fallback_entrypoint:` keys had become DEAD ‚Äî no runtime consumer after the go-quality cutover deleted `initEntrypointArgs`) AND the hardcoded `wellKnownInitDefs` registry (runtime), because the build-time vocab is unavailable at deploy (only the OCI-label init NAME was).

- **New label `ai.opencharly.init_def`** (`labels.go`) carries a dedicated `CapabilityInitDef` JSON subset ‚Äî `entrypoint`, `fallback_entrypoint`, `management_tool`, `management_commands` ‚Äî so build-only `InitDef` fields never leak into the deploy contract. Added per the capabilities recipe: `BoxMetadata.InitDef *CapabilityInitDef` + `CapabilityLabelMap` entry (enforced by `TestCapabilityLabelCompleteness`).
- **Baked at build** in `writeLabels` (`generate.go`) from the vocab-resolved `labelInitDef` (the same `ResolveInitSystem` that already produced `LabelInit`); **read label-first at deploy** ‚Äî `resolveEntrypointFromMeta` (`start.go`) + `resolveInitDefFromMeta` (`service.go`) consult `meta.InitDef` first.
- **`wellKnownInitDefs` retained ONLY as the legacy fallback** for pre-label images (cannot re-bake an already-built image's labels ‚Äî R5 doesn't apply to a still-needed backcompat path); its doc rewritten to say so, and the table frozen (new init systems are declared in the vocab, not added here).
- **Capability win:** the dead vocab `entrypoint:`/`fallback_entrypoint:`/`management_*` keys are now LIVE (consumed ‚Üí label), and **custom init systems declared only in the vocab now work at RUNTIME** (their full contract travels in the label ‚Äî previously "build-only"). The stale "honored at build only" comments + skill notes are corrected.

Runtime class: `golangci-lint` 0, `go build/vet/test` (5 new tests: round-trip, legacy-fallback for supervisord+systemd, custom-init-at-runtime, capability completeness), `task cue:gen` reproducible, `charly box validate`. R8: a freshly-built supervisord image carries the label (`charly box labels ‚Ä¶ --format ai.opencharly.init_def` ‚Üí the resolved entrypoint + management commands) and the deployed quadlet's `Exec=supervisord -n -c /etc/supervisord.conf` derives from it. R10: the `check-pod` disposable bed end-to-end (`PASS`, 10 steps incl. fresh-rebuild; host clean). Bumps the `plugins` gitlink to the matching skill updates.

### 2026-06-20 ‚Äî chore(charly): go-quality cleanup ‚Äî golangci-lint to zero + gofmt

Resolved the full charly Go-quality backlog (the go-quality skill's 1017-issue baseline is STALE ‚Äî the real audit was 13 `golangci-lint` findings + 9 `gofmt` files; the tree has been heavily cleaned since, partly by the CUE-single-source cutover deleting offending code). All fixed MANUALLY (never `golangci-lint --fix` ‚Äî it corrupts this tree) with adversarial default-refute triage:

- **5 staticcheck `QF1012`** (`internal/schemagen`) ‚Üí `fmt.Fprintf` (proven output-stable by `TestGenReproducible`).
- **4 `unconvert`** (`config.go` √ó3, `intermediates.go`) ‚Äî redundant `[]string(...)` on fields already `[]string` (the generated `spec.Box.Build`).
- **1 `unparam` `specSource`** ‚Äî dropped the never-used `[]string` return (both callers discarded it).
- **1 `unparam` `builderPhaseTemplate`** (phase always `PhaseInstall`) ‚Üí `//nolint:unparam` (reasoned): it's the uniform-signature `BuilderDef` analog of `formatPhaseTemplate` (which DOES vary phase via `s.Phase`); the three-phase machinery is documented forward design (`install_build.go:505`), no builder authors `prepare:`/`cleanup:` yet ‚Äî removing the param would delete reachable schema-backed generality.
- **1 `gocyclo` `(*Op).VerbsSet`** (47) ‚Üí `//nolint:gocyclo` (reasoned): the skill's exact flat exactly-one-verb enumeration archetype; extraction would relocate cases without clarifying.
- **1 `unused` `initEntrypointArgs`** ‚Üí DELETED. RCA (skill: an unused unexported func may be a latent missing-caller bug): `git log --all -S "EntrypointArgs("` proves `InitDef.EntrypointArgs` was NEVER wired in any commit (the CUE cutover free-func'd an already-dead method); the runtime entrypoint resolves exclusively from the separate hardcoded `wellKnownInitDefs` registry (`service.go:131`), so the func is unreachable by construction ‚Äî genuinely dead, not a regression.
- **`gofmt -w`** on 9 files (7 test files + `schemagen/main.go` + `spec/hand_state_types.go`) ‚Äî AST-identical.

Gate: `golangci-lint run ./...` = **0 issues**, `gofmt -l .` empty, `go build/vet/test` green, `TestGenReproducible` (pinned cue v0.16.1) byte-identical, `charly box validate`, and the `check-pod` disposable bed end-to-end (`PASS`, 10 steps incl. fresh-rebuild; host clean). No `plugins` change. Candidate follow-up surfaced (non-blocking): the embedded vocab's init `entrypoint:`/`fallback_entrypoint:` keys now have no Go consumer (they were already dead) ‚Äî delete or annotate in a later cutover.

### 2026-06-20 ‚Äî fix(charly): deploy-config state correctness ‚Äî idempotent migrate of a kind-named node + VM-bed entry teardown

Two deploy-config state-handling bugs the prior cutover's R10 surfaced (no authored format change ‚Üí no schema bump):

- **`migrate --dry-run` perpetually (wrongly) reported `would apply unified-node`** on the repo's own root `charly.yml`. RCA: the repo has a node-form entity literally NAMED `vm` (`vm: {vm: {source: ‚Ä¶}}` ‚Äî a valid node-form VM entity whose name collides with the `vm` kind keyword), and `migrateUnifiedNodeDoc` keyed on `legacyKindMapKeys["vm"]` and re-ran the legacy-kind-map rewrite path on it, rebuilding to byte-identical output but returning `changed=true`. Fix (`migrate_unified_node.go`): skip a top-level kind-word entry whose value is ALREADY node-form ‚Äî `!legacyKindMapKeys[k] || (nodeShapedValue(v) && !mapHasKey(v,"name"))`. A genuine legacy collection (`vm: {arch: ‚Ä¶, cachyos: ‚Ä¶}`, entity-name children) is not `nodeShapedValue` and still converts; a legacy single-entity (`vm: {name: ‚Ä¶}`) keeps its `name:` key and still converts. `charly migrate --dry-run` from the repo root now reports `nothing to migrate`.
- **`removeVmDeployEntry` leaked a stale bundle entry** for a `kind: check` VM bed. RCA: a check-VM bed (`check-k3s-vm`) WRITES its `vm_state` under the BUNDLE key (`check-k3s-vm`), but every teardown caller REMOVES the prefixed VM-entity key (`vm:k3s-vm`) ‚Äî an exact-key lookup that missed, so the domain was destroyed but the config entry leaked (and the entry carried no `vm:` cross-ref to resolve it back). Fix (`bundle_add_cmd_vm.go`): `saveVmDeployState` gains a `vmEntity` param and persists `entry.Vm` (the cross-ref linkage); `removeVmDeployEntry` resolves the actual written key(s) via `vmDeployEntryKeys` ‚Äî the literal name AND every bundle whose `vm:` cross-ref names the entity ‚Äî with no over-match.

Runtime class: `go test ./...` (3 new tests incl. node-named-`vm` idempotency, legacy-collection-still-converts, bundle-keyed-entry-removal), `task cue:gen` reproducible, `charly box validate`, repo-root `migrate --dry-run` clean, and the `check-k3s-vm` disposable VM bed end-to-end (`PASS`, 6 phases incl. fresh-rebuild + full k3s suite; **post-teardown the host config has zero `check-k3s-vm` entries** and the fix also cleaned the pre-existing leaked entry; no orphan domain; 8 unrelated entries survived). No `plugins` change.

### 2026-06-20 ‚Äî fix(charly): harden the per-host migrate path ‚Äî empty-dir relocate orphan, testdata skip, vm-state write lock, `ov_install_strategy` key

Follow-up to the CUE-single-source cutover: five per-host migrate-path residuals the R10 bed gate surfaced (none changed an authored wire key).

- **Empty-`~/.config/charly`-dir relocate orphan** (`migrate_charly_rebrand.go`): `relocateHostStateForCharly` retargeted `ctx.HostDeployPath` onto `~/.config/charly` even when the `~/.config/ov ‚Üí ~/.config/charly` move was SKIPPED because `~/.config/charly` already existed (empty), orphaning the real overlay at `~/.config/ov/deploy.yml` and no-op'ing the chain on a phantom path (`charly migrate` silently recovered nothing). New `mergeHostStateDir(from,to)` moves every non-conflicting top-level entry into the empty/lacking target (NEVER clobbering a pre-existing entry) then removes the emptied source ‚Äî so a host in that state recovers with no manual `rmdir`.
- **Migrate walked `charly/testdata`** (non-idempotent dev-repo noise): R3-unified the two duplicated candidate scanners into one `migrateCandidateYAMLFiles` (`migrate_walk.go`) that skips any `testdata` path component (alongside the existing nested-submodule skip); `opUnifyCandidateFiles` + `dropBoxPortCandidateFiles` now delegate to it. ALL doc-migration steps honor the skip (197 candidates, 0 testdata).
- **`saveVmDeployState` lost-update race** (`bundle_add_cmd_vm.go`): the VM-state read-modify-write now takes the same blocking `acquireDeployConfigLock` `saveDeployState`/`cleanDeployEntry` use (applied to `removeVmDeployEntry` too); reentrancy-audited ‚Äî no caller holds the lock, so no self-deadlock (flock per-open-fd).
- **`ov_install_strategy` ‚Üí `charly_install_strategy`** vm_state key (`migrate_install_strategy_key.go`): new `install-strategy-key` migration step at intra-HEAD CalVer `2026.169.0002` (between `unified-node` and `step-venue`) renames the key at every depth on project files AND the per-host overlay; a reflection test pins the rename target to the live `spec.VmDeployState` yaml tag. NO `LatestSchemaVersion` bump ‚Äî this COMPLETES the already-landed 2026.159 ov‚Üícharly rebrand's coverage of an internal deploy-state key, not a new format (HEAD stays `2026.169.0004`; a HEAD bump was empirically proven wrong ‚Äî it breaks `box validate` on the superproject + 5 box submodules already at HEAD).

Runtime class: `go test ./...` (8 new tests incl. concurrent-writers-all-survive, orphan-recovery, testdata-skip, key-rename + struct-tag pin), `task cue:gen` reproducible, `charly box validate`, and the `check-k3s-vm` disposable VM bed end-to-end (`PASS (steps=6)`, the now-locked `persist-auto-port` allocating + persisting + reusing SSH port 44949 with no self-deadlock; host clean after, no orphan domain). Bumps the `plugins` gitlink to the matching migrate-skill note. Two orthogonal pre-existing issues were observed and left for a separate cutover (a `migrateUnifiedNodeDoc` root-`charly.yml` dry-run non-idempotency present on `main`; `removeVmDeployEntry` targeting the `vm:` key not a bundle key).

### 2026-06-20 ‚Äî refactor(charly): CUE `schema/*.cue` is the single source of truth ‚Äî Go param structs + reserved-word vocabulary are GENERATED (gengotypes reversal)

**`charly/schema/*.cue` is now the SINGLE SOURCE OF TRUTH for the `charly.yml` ingress grammar.** The Go param structs, the reserved-word vocabulary, and the kind/verb wiring are GENERATED or DERIVED from the CUE defs ‚Äî there are no hand-maintained parallel copies. `task cue:gen` regenerates the new `charly/spec` package from `charly/schema/*.cue`; `charly/spec/cue_types_gen.go` is emitted by **`cue exp gengotypes`** (then yaml-retagged), and `charly/spec_aliases.go` repoints every package-main param type to its generated twin via `type X = spec.X` (`BoxConfig`, `Op`, `CandyYAML`, `VmSpec`, `ServiceEntry`, ‚Ä¶) so the **Go compiler itself is the field-parity check** ‚Äî a renamed or dropped spec field fails the build at that surface.

**The long-standing do-NOT-use-`gengotypes` guidance is REVERSED.** The former `/charly-internals:go` point-5 rule ("Do NOT generate the Go structs with `cue exp gengotypes` ‚Äî it generalizes disjunctions to `any` and remaps names; keep the hand lockstep instead") no longer holds. The precision loss is handled at the source: every lossy CUE disjunction is annotated `@go(-)` to suppress its generated type, and the faithful Go union/shorthand/state type is hand-written in the SAME `spec` package (`spec/union_types.go`, `spec/scalar_aliases.go`, `spec/hand_state_types.go`) and referenced by name. The committed generated Go can never drift from the schema ‚Äî `charly/spec/gen_repro_test.go` re-runs the exact `task cue:gen` toolchain into a temp dir and diffs against the committed `cue_types_gen.go` + `vocab_gen.go` (skipping gracefully when the pinned `cue` CLI is absent).

**The reserved-word vocabulary + per-verb method allowlists are DERIVED from CUE, and the eight hand vocab lists are DELETED.** `charly/spec/vocab_gen.go` (emitted by the companion generator `charly/internal/schemagen` `-mode=vocab`, via the embedded `cuelang.org/go` API) carries the single-source slices ‚Äî `KindWords`, `ResourceKinds`, `DocDirectives`, `StepKeywords`, `ContextWords`, `DataKeys`, `OpFields`, `OpVerbs`, `AuthoringVerbs`, and the `LiveVerbMethods` allowlist map. The eight hand-maintained lists that previously hard-coded the same words are gone ‚Äî `kindKeys`/`kindKeysSet`, `rootShapeKeys`, `docDirectiveKeys` (`unified.go`) and `nodeEntityKinds`, `nodeResourceKinds`, `nodeStepVerbs`, `nodeDataKeys`, `nodeDocDirectives` (`node_parse.go`) ‚Äî replaced by `kindWordSet` / `resourceKindSet` / `stepKeywordSet` / `dataKeySet` / `docDirectiveSet` set-views in `reserved_registry.go`. The schema concatenation is unified in the new leaf package `charly/internal/schemaconcat`: ONE `ConcatSchema` that both the runtime (`cue_schema.go`'s `sharedCueSchema`) and the dev-time generator call, so the validated schema and the generated types can never diverge.

**A reserved-word‚Üíhandler registry + a startup bijection gate enforce that every kind/verb is wired.** `charly/reserved_registry.go` binds each kind word to its CUE def (`"vm" ‚Üí "#Vm"`), each verb to its `VerbCatalog` entry, and each live-verb method to its `liveVerbDispatch` handler; its `init()` runs three bijection checks fail-fast at process start (mirrored as `TestReservedWordRegistry_{KindBijection,VerbBijection,MethodAllowlists,KindsDispatchable}` in `reserved_registry_test.go`) ‚Äî `checkKindBijection`, `checkVerbBijection`, `checkMethodAllowlists` ‚Äî so a kind/verb/method can no longer be added to the schema without a handler, nor a handler survive its word's deletion.

**`#NodeDoc` is the sole load-time grammar gate; the legacy kind-keyed/root-shape routing and `keylint.go` are DELETED.** `mergeUnifiedDocs` runs every document ‚Äî root `charly.yml` and discovered manifests alike ‚Äî through `classifyDoc` ‚Üí the closed `#NodeDoc` CUE gate ‚Üí `normalizeNodeInto`; a legacy kind-keyed / root-shape document is no longer routed but HARD-REJECTED with a `charly migrate` hint (the `mergeKindDoc` / `firstKindKey` / `VmDoc` routing is removed). The whole `keylint.go` / `keylint_test.go` yaml.v3 `KnownFields` unknown-key linter is deleted ‚Äî CUE's closed-schema check is the real unknown-key gate now, so its self-decoding-types carve-out is gone too. Also deleted: the orphaned `group_spec.go`, `module_spec.go`, `resource_config.go`, `target_spec.go` hand structs the generated `spec` package supersedes.

**No authored wire key changed ‚Äî there is NO schema-version bump and NO `charly migrate` step.** This cutover replaces HOW the grammar is sourced (hand structs + hand vocab lists ‚Üí generated-from-CUE), not the grammar itself: every `charly.yml` that loaded before loads identically after, and the "legacy forms hard-rejected" above are the pre-existing pre-`#NodeDoc` shapes already gated by the unified-node migration, not a new wire change. `LatestSchemaVersion()` stays **`2026.169.0004`** and the migration registry is untouched. Runtime class: `go test ./...` (the `gen_repro` reproducibility gate, the `reserved_registry` bijection gates, the CUE corpus + closedness tests), `task cue:gen` reproducing the committed `spec` package, and `charly box validate` across the superproject + every `box/<distro>` submodule. Bumps the `plugins` gitlink to the matching skill sweep.

### 2026-06-20 ‚Äî fix(chrome-cdp): forward caller flags via "$@" so Chrome's welcome dialog is suppressed and it starts maximized (`v2026.171.0416`)

The `chrome-wrapper` exec block lacked `"$@"`, so the launch flags the supervised `[program:chrome]` service (`selkies-core`) and `chrome-restart` passed were silently DROPPED ‚Äî on the selkies streaming desktops Chrome showed its first-run "welcome / make default" dialog and opened un-maximized. Fix: the launch flags now live in the wrapper itself (single source) and `"$@"` forwards any caller flags; `chrome-restart` and the `selkies-core` chrome service are simplified to call the bare wrapper. The old callers' `--force-renderer-accessibility` (inert under the dropped-flags bug, so production Chrome never actually had it) is intentionally NOT restored ‚Äî CDP automation does not need forced renderer a11y. Adds 3 deterministic `selkies-core` checks that FAIL without the fix: `selkies-core-chrome-launch-flags` (`--no-first-run` + `--start-maximized` in the live `/proc/<pid>/cmdline`), `selkies-core-chrome-maximized` (CDP-measured window ‚âà screen ‚Üí `MAXOK`, proving maximize took effect not merely the flag), `selkies-core-frame-not-uniform` (real composited frame, not a black void ‚Äî closes the same false-green gap the `agent-check` leaves under `--no-agent`). Verified on the `check-selkies-labwc-pod` bed (180 steps, 0 failed; all 3 new checks PASS on a fresh rebuild) + a live screenshot of the maximized welcome-free Chrome. The selkies-KDE flavor has a separate no-systemd-user session instability that blocks ITS bed (HELD as a dedicated effort ‚Äî see the `selkies-kde-kwin-instability` memory: systemd1 `/bin/false` storm + wl-paste/wlr-data-control leak both fixed there, chrome CDP `unix_wait_for_peer` needs a real systemd-user); this fix is the shared chrome candy, proven on the labwc flavor. candy `chrome-cdp` ‚Üí 2026.170.2101, `selkies-core` ‚Üí 2026.170.2327.

### 2026-06-19 ‚Äî fix(kde-selkies): launch plasmashell explicitly so the streamed Plasma desktop renders (panel + wallpaper) (`v2026.170.2016`)

The selkies-kde streaming desktop showed only the Chrome window on a BLACK void ‚Äî no Plasma panel/wallpaper. RCA (RDD-proven on the live `check-selkies-kde-pod` bed): Plasma 6's `startplasma-wayland` delegates workspace bring-up to the systemd USER session; a supervisord pod has none, so startplasma's legacy `plasma_session` fallback starts only kwin+kded and NEVER launches plasmashell (the `X-systemd-skip=true` autostart layer it lives in). Fix: `kde-selkies-session` backgrounds `startplasma-wayland`, polls for kwin's `wayland-0` client socket, then launches `plasmashell` on it explicitly ‚Äî the KDE analogue of how the labwc flavor launches its panel. Adds the deterministic `kde-selkies-plasmashell-running` check (`pgrep -x plasmashell`): it FAILS on the old launcher and PASSES on the fix, closing the coverage hole that let the bug ship green (the frame-content `agent-check` runs `--no-agent` in beds). Proven: bed PASS on a fresh rebuild + a live screenshot of the full Breeze desktop. candy `kde-selkies` version ‚Üí 2026.170.1959.

### 2026-06-19 ‚Äî feat(charly)!: unified name-first node model for all of charly.yml + GPU auto-preemptible arbitration (`v2026.170.1105`)

charly.yml collapses to ONE name-first node model ‚Äî every entity, bundle member,
plan step, and data field is a `<name>: {<kind>: ‚Ä¶, <child-nodes>}` node, one
`#Node` CUE schema at every depth (CLOSED, fully validated before anything
executes). `deploy:`‚Üí`bundle:`, `charly deploy`‚Üí`charly bundle`,
`DeploymentNode`‚Üí`BundleNode`. Venue + membership now come from TREE POSITION ‚Äî
the authored `on:`/`pod:`(step)/`peer:`/`nested:`/`target:` keys are REMOVED; a
step nested under a member runs on that member, a resource node placed under
another deploys into it. `${HOST:<member>}` (`:<port>` for a host-reachable
endpoint) is the SOLE cross-member address, superseding
`${PEER_HOST}`/`${PEER_ENDPOINT}`. A new `agent_provisioned: true` tree-child flag
marks agent-built bed pods (foldMembers skips them ‚Äî the iterate-benchmark
contract). An idempotent `charly migrate` step (+ registry HEAD bump) synthesizes
all of it from any legacy config. CUE stays the closed schema authority.

GPU resource-arbitration robustness: a pod that USES the nvidia GPU device
auto-claims `requires_shared:[nvidia-gpu]` (`acquireResourceForClaimant` ‚Üí
`withImpliedGPUShared`), so EVERY GPU consumer is a tracked, preemptable shared
claimant with no per-deploy config ‚Äî the `requires_exclusive:` arbiter then
gracefully preempts them and flips nvidia‚Üívfio fully automatically. The switch's
EBUSY refusal now NAMES the external holder (`formatNvidiaHolders` /
`discoverNvidiaHolders`) instead of a cryptic message.

R10 (fresh rebuild, RTX 4080): `check-cross-pod-cdp` PASS; `check-selkies-kde-nvidia-vm`
from-box nested-pod deploy + nvidia‚Üívfio switch + in-guest GPU live-proven; a
`gpu-holder` ordinary pod auto-claimed + preempted on-card; full bed roster (24
beds + 3 cross beds) proven on the unified loader; `charly box validate` exit 0
across all 6 repos; `go test`/`golangci` green. Known immediate-next cutovers:
box-submodule candy `@github` pins ‚Üí `charly box reconcile` to this tag; the
selkies-kde desktop stream (:3000) needs GSettings schemas + an
xdg-desktop-portal rootless-fuse fix (a selkies-kde candy issue, not this change).
